+Jamison Brereton

86 (798)
Soma Pavama╠Дna
Akrс╣гс╣н─Б ╠е s, the M─Бс╣г─Б seer-group (1тАУ10); Siktat─Бs, the Niv─Бvar─л seer-group (11тАУ20); Pr┼Ы╠е nis, the Aj─Б seer-group (21тАУ30); Atris (31тАУ40); Atri Bhauma (41тАУ45); Grtsam ╠е ada (46тАУ48) 48 verses: jagat─л, arranged in trcas ╠е
As noted in the introduction to IX.85, this last hymn of the jagat─л group, one of the longest in the R╠еgveda, can actually be easily divided into smaller hymns, in this case into sixteen sets of tr╠еcas, and can thus be made to conform to the patterns of hymn arrangement. The resulting triadic groupings do not at all match the divisions in the Anukramaс╣З─л reproduced above. The degree of internal cohesion between tr╠еcas varies considerably: some show no obvious signs of unity, while others (e.g., vss. 28тАУ30) are stylistically unified. There is also some chaining across tr╠еca boundar
ies; for example, verse 4, which begins the second tr╠еca, is strictly parallel to verses 1 and 2 (especially the former). Such chaining is not an argument against the tr╠еca division, as perceived similarities between particular tr╠еcas might have dictated the arrangement of originally separate hymns. The last tr╠еca (vss. 46тАУ48), attributed to Gr╠еtsamada, ends with the Gr╠еtsamada clan refrain of Maс╣Зс╕Нala II.
That said, the impression this sprawling collection gives is of an agglomeration of soma-hymn clich├йs, many of which are repeated with little or no variation at irregular intervals throughout the тАЬhymn.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted above, an assemblage consisting of 16 three-vs. units, attributed to a variety of poets and poetic groups and showing no particular unity of structure or special poetic merit. However, there is often patterned repetition both between tс╣Ыcas and within them.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYour (juices), purified (Soma), all-pervading, quick as thought, go of themselves like the offspring of swift (mares); the celestial well-winged sweet-flavoured juices, great exciters of exhilaration, alight upon the receptacle.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Forth do your swift exhilarating drinks, sped by insights, rush, o self-purifying one, like the swift-born (birds) themselves.
The heavenly, fine-feathered, honeyed drops, most exhilarating, take their seats around the cask.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The rt noun cmpd dh─л-j┼л╠Б- (also in vs. 4) could have two different readings, тАШsped by insight(s)тАЩ and тАШspeeding insightsтАЩ; see Scarlatta 170-71. The published translation opts for the passive interpr., as does Renou, while Geldner chooses the transitive one. Either is possible in this ritual context, and parallels cut both ways. On the one hand, there is the parallel cmpd dh─л-j├бvana- (3x), which must have transitive value; on the other,

+Griffith

THY gladdening draughts, O Pavamana, urged by song flow swiftly of themselves like sons of fleet-foot mares.
The drops of Soma juice, those eagles of the heavens, most cheering, rich in meath, rest in the reservoir.

+Geldner

Deine raschen, gedankenweckenden Rauschtr├дnke rinnen , o Pavamana, leibhaftig wie die von Rennern erzeugten Rosse voran. Die himmlischen Adler, die s├╝├Яen S├дfte, die berauschendsten umlagern die Kufe.

+Grassmann

Vor str├╢men deine raschen S├дfte, Flammender, gedankenschnell, wie von dem fl├╝cht’gen Aar erzeugt, Die honigs├╝ssen Indu’s, die berauschendsten, des Himmels V├╢gel sitzen auf der Kufe rings.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYour exhilarating, all-pervading juices are let loose separately like chariot-horses; the sweet-flavoured (Soma) waves (go) to Indra the wilder of the thunderbolt as a cow with her milk to the calf.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Forth have your swift, exhilarating, invigorating drinks surged, like chariot-horses, each separately.
As a milk-cow (goes) to her calf with milk, the drops, the honeyed
waves (go) to Indra, possessor of the mace.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

It seems a little odd to say that chariot horses go тАЬeach separately,тАЭ since one would think that the horses would be attached to the same chariot and efficient movement would require them to pull together. But almost the same phrase occurs in X.91.7 тАж rathy├▓ y├бth─Б pс╣Ы╠Бthak, though there referring to charioteers, and so the words must belong together. Perhaps it refers to separate chariots, each with its own set of horsesтАФor that each horse in a chariot team has its own place in harness and each individually contributes to the speed of the whole?

+Griffith

As rapid chariot-steeds, so turned in several ways have thine exhilarating juices darted forth,
Soma-drops rich in meath, waves, to the Thunder-armed, to Indra, like milch-kine who seek their calf with milk.

+Geldner

Deine berauschenden raschen Rauschtr├дnke haben sich einzeln in Lauf gesetzt wie Wagenrosse. Wie die Kuh mit der Milch zum Kalbe kommen die S├дfte, die s├╝├Яen Wogen zum Keulentr├дger Indra.

+Grassmann

Ergossen haben deine raschen S├дfte sich, die lustigen wie Wagenrosse weit und breit, Des Indutrankes honigs├╝sse Wellen hin zum Blitzer Indra, wie zum Kalb mit Milch die Kuh.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬLike a horse urged on to battle, do you who are all-knowing rush from heaven to the receptacle whose mother is the cloud; Soma the showerer (of benefits) is being purified at the top upon the woollen filter for Indra’s strength which supports (the world).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

For Indra’s strength: dh─Бyase = dh─Бrak─Бya; or, ’to Indra’s supporting’, i.e. to support Indra

+Jamison Brereton

Like a steed being spurred, rush to the prize, to the cask of heaven, whose mother is the stoneтАФ
you, the finder of the sun, the bullish Soma, being purified in the filter, on the sheepтАЩs back, for IndraтАЩs suckling.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda a is metrically disturbed, despite apparently having 12 syl. With Arnold and Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition, best to read *hy─Бn├бс╕е for hiy─Бn├бс╕е (as sometimes elsewhere), to avoid a too early or too late caesura and a bad Jagat─л cadence. The p─Бda is then a fine Triс╣гс╣нubh.

Although, as noted above, vss. 1 and 3 share the same goal, the k├│┼Ыa-, the physical referent has changed between 1 and 3. In the former, the cask is presumably the soma vessel on the ritual ground, but in 3b it is characterized as k├│┼Ыaс╣Г div├│ ├бdrim─Бtaram тАЬthe cask of heaven, whose mother is the stoneтАЭтАФin other words the vault of the sky (or the soma container in the sky). So the subject is the heavenly soma, not merely the ritual substance, even though the ritual details are re-asserted in cd. For the heavenly cask, see V.53. 6, 59.8, IX.88.6. Oldenberg reports without enthusiasm a potential emendation to nom. ├бdrim─Бt─Б, modifying soma, with ├бdri- the pressing stone. This would yield another Triс╣гс╣нubh p─Бda. However, since heaven (or at least the container of the heavenly soma) may be made of stone, there seems no reason to emend.

In the published translation for ease of English parsing I moved the tr. of svarv├нd from b to cd, but this mixes the levels: the sun-finding Soma is the one that reaches heaven, while the soma of cd is the substance purified in the sheepтАЩs filter. Better (if somewhat awkward): тАЬтАж rush to the prize, as the sun-finder (rush) to the cask of heaven тАжтАЭ

+Griffith

Like a steed urged to battle, finder of the light; speed onward to the cloud-born reservoir of heaven,
A Steer that o’er the woolly surface seeks the sieve, Soma while purified for Indra’s nourishment.

+Jamison Brereton

Forth have your heavenly (hymns), sped by insight, destined for the A┼Ыvins, surged with their milk into the support, o self-purifying one.
Forth within (the support) have the seers sent their substantial (hymns) surgingтАФthose ritual experts who groom you, o you who win
seers [?].

+Jamison Brereton Notes

As just noted, this vs. seems to distill the first tс╣Ыca and is esp. similar to vs. 1. Like both 1 and 2 it opens pr├б te, and the 2nd hemistich also begins with pr├б, with pr─Б╠Бnt├бr echoing pr├б ta). Even more strikingly the first p─Бda matches 1a almost exactly: 1a pr├б ta ─Б┼Ы├бvaс╕е pavam─Бna dh─лj├бvaс╕е 4a pr├б ta ─Б╠Б┼Ыvin─лс╕е pavam─Бna dh─лj├бvaс╕е The only difference is the third word, and the two are phonological multiforms of each other - or rather, ─Б╠Б┼Ыvin─лс╕е must have been formed as a variant of ─Б┼Ы├бvaс╕е, since the vс╣Ыddhi deriv. ─Б╠Б┼Ыvina-, -─л is found only here in the RV (though it occurs elsewhere in Vedic), while ─Б┼Ы├║- is quite common. In addition, asс╣Ыgran (4b) and asс╣Ыkс╣гata (4c) reprise ├бsс╣Ыkс╣гata of 2b, and p├бyas─Б (4b) recurs from 2c.

However, these similarities once again mask conceptual differences.

The first question to confront is what the referents are for the fem. pls. ─Б╠Б┼Ыvin─лс╕е in p─Бda a and sth─Б╠Бvir─лс╕е in c, and are they the same? Geldner and Renou both supply different nouns for the two - dh─Б╠Бr─Бс╕е тАШstreamsтАЩ for the first (already S─Бyaс╣Зa.) and g├нraс╕е тАШhymnsтАЩ for the second. (S─Бyaс╣Зa. supplies dh─Б╠Бr─Бс╕е for the second as well.) Although this split reference is perfectly possible - and at least p├бyas─Б тАШwith their milkтАЩ might favor a liquid interpretation in ab - I prefer to supply g├нraс╕е for both. In the 2nd hemistich the passage adduced by Oldenberg to explain p─Бda c, I.181.7 ├бsarji v─Бm sth├бvir─Б vedhas─Б g─л╠Бс╕е тАЬA substantial song has been sent surging to you, o ritual experts,тАЭ resembles our passage very closely, with fem. g─л╠Бс╕е and with verb, adj., and voc. matching elements in cd. There is only one fem. form to the adj. sth├бvira-, namely the one just cited modifying g├нr-. The pleonastically+++(=redundant)+++ vс╣Ыddhied adj. in our passage, fem. sth─Б╠Бvir─л-, is a hapax in the RV - and in fact I would suggest that it owes its vс╣Ыddhi to an attempt to match that of ─Б╠Б┼Ыvin─лс╕е. Moreover, I.181.7 passage is in an A┼Ыvin hymn (the referents of v─Бm тАж vedhas─Б), and to my mind the unusual ─Б╠Б┼Ыvin─лс╕е тАШdestined for the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ in the first hemistich invites us to supply a form of praise as the fem. pl. referent. We might also cite other exx. of the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ association with praise hymns (not, I realize, unusual for Vedic gods!): VII.72.3 st├│m─Бso a┼Ыv├нnoс╕е, VIII.9.7 a┼Ыv├нnoс╕е … st├│mam, VIII.9.16 v─Бc─Б╠Б…. a┼Ыv├нnaс╕е (though none of these is fem. pl.). Thus in my view the entities тАЬdestined for the A┼ЫvinsтАЭ in p─Бda a are more likely to be hymns than streams.

In the first hemistich the fem. subj. (whatever it is) surges тАЬinto the supportтАЭ (dh├бr─лmaс╣Зi), which I take to be the soma vessel. I supply the same loc. with ant├бr in the 2nd hemistich. Cf. nearby IX.89.5 sam─Бn├й ant├бr dhar├║с╣Зe n├нс╣гattaс╕е тАЬset down within the same support,тАЭ with dhar├║с╣Зe an etymological and semantic match for dh├бr─лman-.

As noted above, asс╣Ыkс╣гata in c repeats ├бsс╣Ыkс╣гata in 2b, but they are functional opposites: the first verb must be intrans. тАШhave surgedтАЩ (or pass., тАШhave been dischargedтАЩ) with the soma drinks as subject, while our verb is trans. with the seers as subj. and hymns as obj. The intrans/pass.. function is taken over in vs. 4 by asс╣Ыgran in b. The aor. of тИЪsс╣Ыj is overwhelmingly medial and overwhelmingly intrans./pass. in function, including the numerous exx. of 3rd pl. ├бsс╣Ыkс╣гata. There are only two transitive occurrences of this form, this one and one in V.52.6. In our case I think it likely that in this vs. asс╣Ыkс╣гata has been made to contrast functionally with likewise 3rd pl. asс╣Ыgran, which patterns with the aor. passive and therefore has more title to intrans./pass. function. Narten (Sig.Aor. 270-71) discusses the functional issues in the s-aor. paradigm of this root, but she holds the (to me) unlikely position that the medial forms should be fundamentally transitive (though she hedges here) and the intrans. use is secondary, despite the clear numerical superiority of the intrans. usage. I think it makes more sense to consider the transitive usage, at least here, as forced on a normally intrans. form by the pressure of asс╣Ыgran.

The formation of the hapax voc. с╣Ыс╣гiс╣г─Бс╣Зa is opaque. GrassmannтАЩs gloss тАШdem S├дnger freundтАЩ reveals nothing about his analysis of the 2nd part; sim. RenouтАЩs тАШpropre aux Proph├иtesтАЩ without further comment. With Geldner, the published translation assigns the 2nd member to тИЪsan тАШgain, winтАЩ, hence тАШwinning seersтАЩ. If we maintain that analysis, the sense might be compared to с╣Ыс╣гi-s├бh- in IX.76.4, which means тАШvanquishing (the other) seersтАЩ, in poetic competition or the like. However, given the seс╣н nature of тИЪsan and the persistent short vowel (-)san- in most of its nominal forms, this analysis is not entirely persuasive, esp. since the semantics are not absolutely compelling. AiG II.2.926 posits (without conviction) a suffix -s─Бna-, but also suggests a connection to the (pseudo-)part. -as─Бna- type (which is treated at AiG II.2.236-37), but it doesnтАЩt fit the general profile of this group (on which see comm. ad IV.3.6). Perhaps -s─Бnais better connected to тИЪs─Б тАШbindтАЩ; cf. the noun viс╣г─Б╠Бna- V.44.11, which has the merit of existing and whose long vowel is predictable. Hence тАШbinding seersтАЩ or тАШhaving the binding of seersтАЩ - that is, holding them fast, commanding their loyalty or attention, as in p─Бda c. But in the absence of any further information, accentual, contextual, or formulaic, we canтАЩt get much further.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAll-seeing (Soma), the mighty rays of you, who are the lord, encompass all the sphere; pervading (all things) you flow, Soma, through your functions; you rule lord of the whole world.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Through your functions: ‘by the supporting streams of juice’

+Jamison Brereton

Your beacons circle around all the domains, though you are in
advanceтАФyou ingenious one whose gaze is on all.
Reaching through (the domains), you purify yourself, Soma, according to your ordinances. You rule as lord of all creation.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

As should be clear from the immed. preceding discussion, as elsewhere in IX I take dh─Б╠Бm─Бni тАШdomainsтАЩ as referring to the filter and subsequent locales that the soma traverses, not, with Geldner, SomaтАЩs forms. (What Renou means by тАЬstructuresтАЭ is uninterpretable to me.) The physical locations on the ritual ground can also be viewed as the cosmic domains over which Soma has dominion - hence the hyperbolic statement in d, attributing universal rule to Soma.

On v├н┼Ыvasya bh├║vanasya r─Бjasi, see the identical phrase in 28b.

vy─Бna┼Ы├н- belongs with the redupl. -├н-stem type of cakr├н-, etc. (cf. weak pf. vy─Б╠Аna┼Ы- to тИЪ(n)a┼Ы); see AiG II.2.292. It can therefore govern the acc., like other instances of this formation type, and we can easily supply dh─Б╠Бm─Бni from p─Бda a, strongly supported by the parallel later in the hymn: IX.86.15 y├│ asya dh─Б╠Бma pratham├бс╣Г vy─Бna┼Ыe тАЬwho has reached through his first domain,тАЭ with the medial perfect to v├н тИЪ(n)a┼Ы.

+Griffith

O thou who seest all things, Sovran as thou art and passing strong, thy rays encompass all abodes.
Pervading with thy natural powers thou flowest on, and as the whole world’s Lord, O Soma, thou art King.

+Geldner

Der du der Gebieter bist, deine, des Meisters, Banner durchlaufen alle deine Formen, o Allseher. Durchdringend l├дuterst du dich, o Soma, nach den Vorschriften. Als Gebieter herrschst du ├╝ber die ganze Welt.

+Grassmann

Allsehender, es dringen deine Strahlen rings um alle St├дtten, der du k├╝hn und kr├дftig bist, Durchdringend rieselst, Soma, du nach deinem Brauch, als K├╢nig herrschst du ├╝ber diese ganze Welt.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe rays, the tokens of the extant, steady, purified Soma, circulate from both worlds; when the green-tinted juice is cleansed upon the filter, reposing it alights upon its station, the pitchers.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The rays, the beacons of the self-purifying one circle around on both sides, though he stays fixed.
When the fallow bay is groomed in the filter, seated in his womb, he sits down in the tubs.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The referent changes from 2nd ps. (vs. 5) to 3rd (vs. 6), although this is not clear until the 3rd sg. verbs in the 2nd hemistich.

тАЬOn both sidesтАЭ (ubhay├бtaс╕е) probably reflects the double reference just noted: the ritual and the cosmic, or the earthly and the heavenly. See Geldner n. 6ab.

I read y├бd─л as y├бd ─л (with enclitic prn.), since тАЬifтАЭ does not work well here.

+Griffith

The beams of Pavamana, sent from earth and heaven, his ensigns who is ever steadfast, travel round.
When on the sieve the Golden-hued is cleansed, he rests within the vats as one who seats him in his place.

+Geldner

Des Pavamana Strahlen, seine Banner wandeln auf beiden Seiten um, w├дhrend er fest bleibt. Wenn der Falbe in der Seihe sauber gemacht wird, setzt sich der gern Sitzende an seinen Platz, in die Kr├╝ge.

+Grassmann

Nach beiden Seiten dringen seine Strahlen durch, der flammend rieselt, fest und treu in seinem Sinn, Wenn in dem Sieb das goldne Ross gestriegelt wird, so setzt es in die Kufen sich auf seinen Sitz.

+Elizarenkova

+Jamison Brereton

Having a thousand streams, he rushes around the cask. The bull keeps bellowing as he goes across the filter.

+Griffith

He speeds with thousand currents to the reservoir, and passes through the filter bellowing as a bull.

тАЬThe royal (Soma) plural nges into the firmament, (and) the rivers (thereof), mixed with the streams, he associates with the wave of the waters; being filtered he stands upon the uplifted woollen (filter) on the navel of the earth, the upholder of the vast heaven.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Navel of the earth: yaj├▒am─Бhu bhuvanasya n─Бbhim: Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б 7.4.18.2; associate with the wave of the waters: to indicate the effect of the Soma in producing rain by combining in the clouds with the solar rays

+Jamison Brereton

The king plunges through the sea, the rivers. Fixed in the streams he accompanies the wave of waters.

High heaven’s Sustainer at the central point of earth, raised on the fleecy surface Pavamana stands.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThundering like the summit of the sky (the Soma) roars, by whose support both heaven and earth, (are upheld); the Soma flows acquiring Indra’s friendship, purified he alights upon the pitchers.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Thundering like the back of heaven he has roared, he according to whose ordinances both heaven and earth (abide).
He purifies himself, always finding the fellowship of Indra. Soma, while being purified, sits in the tubs.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The rel. cl. of b lacks a verb. I think that whatever is supplied must be able to be construed with dh├бrmabhiс╕е тАЬaccording to (his) ordinances.тАЭ My тАШabideтАЩ is a slight elaboration on GeldnerтАЩs тАШsindтАЩ: тАЬdurch dessen Bestimmungen Himmel und Erde sind,тАЭ which I think is fundamentally correct. This is another hyperbolic statement of SomaтАЩs cosmic power. RenouтАЩs тАЬlui ├а qui (appartiennent) le ciel et la terre avec les choses-├а-maintenirтАЭ separates y├бsya from dh├бrmabhiс╕е and finds little work for the instr. pl. to do. The two instances of dh├бrmabhiс╕е (here and 5c) should be more or less in harmony.

+Griffith

He on whose high decree the heavens and earth depend nath roared and thundered like the summit of the sky.
Soma flows on obtaining Indra’s friendly love, and, as they purify him, settles in the jars.

+Geldner

Donnernd wie des Himmels R├╝cken hat er sein Gebr├╝ll erhoben, durch dessen Bestimmungen Himmel und Erde sind. Er l├дutert sich, der Indra┬┤s Freundschaft genau kennt; sich l├дuternd setzt sich Soma in den Kr├╝gen.

+Grassmann

Jetzt br├╝llte donnernd wie des Himmels Gipfel er, in dessen Ordnung Himmel sich und Erde f├╝gt; Des Indra Freundschaft sich gewinnend rieselt er, gereinigt setzet Soma in die Kufen sich.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe light of the sacrifice, he distils sweet (juice) delightful (to the gods), the parent of the gods, the genitive rator (of all), possessed of ample wealth; he supports the hidden wealth of heaven and earth, the most exhilarating, the exciting (Soma), the nourisher of (Indra), the juice.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Light of the sacrifice, he purifies himself as its dear honey, the father, begetter of the gods, possessing conspicuous goods.
He establishes a secret treasure in the two independent powers
[=Heaven and Earth], as the most invigorating exhilarating
Indrian sap.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner notes the parallels between our vs. and IX.75.2: IX.75.2a. тАж pavate m├бdhu priy├бm, тАж 2cd d├бdh─Бti putr├бс╕е pitr├│r ap─лcy├аm, n─Б╠Бma тАж IX.86.10a тАж pavate m├бdhu priy├бm, тАж .10c d├бdh─Бti r├бtnaс╣Г svadh├бyor ap─лcy├аm But he doesnтАЩt seem to take the parallelism too seriously. In particular, though both 75.2c and 86.10c have a dual gen./loc. to be construed with a VP in which the subject deposits / establishes a secret X [name in 75.2, treasure in 86.10], Geldner takes the dual as loc. in 75.2 (where thereтАЩs a parallel loc. sg. rocan├й), but gen. here (тАЬEr bringt das verborgene Kleinod der beiden Eigenm├дchteтАЭ)(sim. Renou), with a somewhat forced interpr. of d├бdh─Бti as тАШbringtтАЩ. Since the dual seems to have the same referent in both passages, Heaven and Earth (so both Geldner and Renou), and the passages are otherwise so similar, it seems to me very likely that they are structured in the same way. I therefore take svadh├бyoс╕е as loc. ItтАЩs worth noting that this is the only du. form of the stem svadh─Б╠Б-

тАЬIn the front of the waters rushes the filtered (Soma), foremost (he rushes) in the front of the voice, he goes among the rays; in the front he engages in battle (to win) food; well-armed, the showerer (of benefits), he is purified by the offerers of the oblation.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

At the forefront of the rivers, purifying himself he rushes; at the forefront of speech he goes foremost among the cows.
At the forefront of the prize(-contest) he takes great stakes as his share. The bull of good weapons is purified by the pressers.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThis (Soma) possessed of agreeable (praise) filtered, and sent forth, (quick) as a bird goes with a stream (of juice) through the fleece; by your sustaining act, by your intelligence, sage Indra, the pure Soma flows purified through both heaven and earth.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

This one here, accompanied by thought, like a bird spurred on has run into the sheepтАЩs (fleece), purifying himself in a wave.
By your resolve, o sage poet, by your insight, the clear Soma purifies himself between the two world-halves for you, o Indra.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner identifies (n. 13a) and tr. mat├бv─Бn as a real past active participle (тАЬNachdem er sich bedacht hatte тАжтАЭ)(sim. L├╝ders 243). This seems highly unlikely to me; WhitneyтАЩs statement (Grassmann ┬з960) should be noted: тАЬDerivative words of this formation [=-t├бvant- sj] are found in RV., but without anything like a participial value. The AV. has a single example тАж In the Br─Бhmaс╣Зas also it is hardly met with.тАЭ See also RenouтАЩs n. The fact that the base, mat├б-, is not found independently as a ppl. in the RV, but only once (besides here) in the cmpd. matavacas- (voc., so unaccented, I.46.5), makes the building of a past active part. to it even less likely. Instead -vantmust have its usual possessive sense and in context mean тАШaccompanied by thoughtsтАЩ (like mar├║tvant-), referring to the praises given to Soma at the ritual. These act as a spur to set the soma in motion, hence the following simile.

The 2nd hemistich opens with a form of the 2nd sg prn., t├бva, followed at intervals by two vocc., kave at the end of c and indra in d, followed immediately by vs.-final te. It only becomes clear in d, with the 3rd ps. phrase pavate s├│maс╕е, that the 2nd ps. cannot be Soma, as it was earlier in the hymn (vss. 1-3, 4-5). The kave is a bit of a red herring, since it could, and often does, refer to Soma, and though Indra is sometimes so designated, other gods are far more commonly so called. The voc. indra at the end settles the matter, but our poet seems to tease us with other possibilities.

The image of Soma purifying himself тАЬbetween the two world-halvesтАЭ of course reflects the cosmic reach of the Soma, but it may also have a narrower ritual application. In IX.98.9 Geldner suggests that the world-halves there are the jaws of the soma-press, which would fit nicely here. See also IX.75.4, where the world-halves are called the mothers of Soma.

+Griffith

This heedful Pavamana, like a bird sent forth, hath with his wave flowed onward to the fleecy sieve.
O Indra, through thy wisdom, b thy thought, O Sage, Soma flows bright and pure between the earth and heaven.

+Geldner

Nachdem er sich bedacht hatte, ist dieser wie ein Vogel getrieben mit der Woge auf die Schafwolle geeilt, sich l├дuternd. Zwischen beiden Welten wird nach deinem Sinne, o Seher, mit Kunst, o Indra, der reine Soma f├╝r dich gel├дutert.

+Grassmann

Sein Ziel verfolgend, wie ein Falke ausgesandt ergoss er rieselnd auf die Wolle wogend sich; Durch deinen Antrieb, weiser Indra, rieselt hell mit Einsicht Soma zwischen Erd’ und Himmel dir.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWearing a coat of mail reaching to heaven, the adorable Soma, who fills the firmament (with rain), plural ced in the waters, genitive rating heaven,passes with the water, (and) worships its ancient parent (Indra).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Wearing a coat of mail: i.e., clothed in light

+Jamison Brereton

Clothing himself in a mantle that touches heaven, the one worthy of the sacrifice, filling the midspace, is fitted into the worlds.
While being born, he has stridden along the cloud toward the sun; he wishes to entice his age-old father here.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I would now tr. the pf. part. jaj├▒─Бn├бс╕е with past value, тАЬonce having been born.тАЭ The standard tr. (and incl. Ober II.76; Lowe, Part. 158) take sv├бr as nom. with the pf. part.: тАЬhaving been born as the sun.тАЭ This is of course quite possible. But I would expect a goal with abh├н тИЪkram and therefore take sv├аr as acc. in that function (see also Scarlatta 330).

I take n├бbhas─Б as instr. of extent of space, rather than accompaniment (Geldner, Lowe) or, even less likely, agent (Renou тАЬsтАЩest ├йlanc├й par la nu├йe,тАЭ despite the absence of any verbal form that could be interpr. as passive).

The identify of the тАЬage-old fatherтАЭ isnтАЩt clear, and various candidates have been suggested: S─Бyaс╣Зa.: Indra; Geldner (n. 14d): Parjanya or Heaven; Renou: Heaven. IтАЩm generally inclined towards Heaven, though of course bringing Heaven here is not physcially possible.

+Griffith

He, clad in mail that reaches heaven, the Holy One, filling the firmament stationed amid the worlds,
Knowing. the realm of light, hath come to us in rain: he summons to himself his own primeval Sire.

+Geldner

Einen Mantel umlegend, der zum Himmel reicht, den Luftraum erf├╝llend, ├╝ber die Wolken gesetzt, der Opferw├╝rdige, als Sonne geboren, ist er mit der Wolke darauf losgegangen. Er w├╝nscht seinen uralten Vater herbei.

+Grassmann

Ins Kleid geh├╝llt, der hehre, das zum Himmel reicht, die Luft erf├╝llend, in die Wesen eingef├╝gt, Erzeugt durch Fluten, schritt er jetzt zum Himmel hin, erfreuet seinen urgebornen Vater nun.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬ(Soma), who first reached Indra’s glorious body, gives great happiness to the entrance of Indra (that Soma), whose station is in the highest heaven, and through whom (Indra) triumphs in all contests.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Through whom: ataс╕е = yasm─Бt som─Бt (tс╣Ыpta indraс╕е); ‘since his (Soma’s) station is in the highest heaven, therefore he (Soma) triumphs’

+Jamison Brereton

He extends his great shelter to the clan, when he has reached through his first domain.
What is his footprint in the highest distant heavenтАФfrom that he proceeds toward all the (streams) in uninterrupted array.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

In d note the play in the phrase s├бс╣Г y─Бti saс╣Гy├бtaс╕е, which belong to different roots (тИЪy─Б and тИЪyat respectively). тАШfeste AufstellungтАЩ. +Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYour thoughtful worshippers (Soma), desiring an exhilarating sound, purposing praise, advance into the halls of sacrifice; the praisers the lords of intellect praise Soma, the kine approach him with their milk.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Forth have your insights stridden, arousing exhilaration, expressing admiration, inviting admiration in their joint dwellings.
The inspired thoughts, the rhythms have roared to Soma; the milk-cows have mixed him with milk.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The published translation does not make it clear that тАЬyourтАЭ is pl. (enclitic vaс╕е) and must refer to the poet/officiants.

What is striking stylistically in this vs. is the sequence of three heavy nom. pl.

fem. -yu-adjectives: mandray├║vo vipany├║vaс╕е, panasy├║vaс╕е, the latter two derived from the same root. Though morphologically parallel, they are somewhat disharmonious: mandray├║- is a hapax, vipany├║- is reasonably well attested and generally modifies the human officiants (gods a few times), while the rather fewer occurrences of panasy├║- (and the related verb panasy├б-) refer to gods. Hence the тАЬthoughtsтАЭ of our vs. seem both to тАЬexpress admiration,тАЭ as humans do to gods, and тАЬinvite/require admiration,тАЭ as gods do from humans - so the thoughtsтАЩ purposes seem to be various, both to praise the gods and be admired for their fine crafting? IтАЩm not exactly sure what saс╣Гv├бsana- (a hapax), lit. тАШdwelling together, joint dwellingтАЩ is expressing here. Geldner seems similarly puzzled, tr. тАЬin den SitzungenтАЭ with a question mark; RenouтАЩs тАЬdans les sessions-rituellesтАЭ is more definite and appealing, but I donтАЩt see where he gets it. Perhaps it doesnтАЩt indicate that the thoughts are dwelling with each other but that they, as a group, are dwelling with something/-one else - perhaps the soma, perhaps the milk and other non-verbal parts of the ritual machinery?

+Griffith

Your songs, exhilarating, tuneful, uttering praise, are come into the placns where the people meet.
Worshippers have exalted Soma with their hymns, and milch kine have come near to meet him with their milk.

+Geldner

Eure Dichtungen huben an, wohlklingend, lobspendend in den Sitzungen, nach Beifall verlangend. Dem Soma t├╢nten die Dichtungen, die Ges├дnge entgegen. Die Milchk├╝he haben ihn mit ihrer Milch gemischt.

+Grassmann

Jetzt schritten eure frommen Andachtswerke vor, erfreuend, r├╝hmend und bewundernd bei dem Fest, Dem Soma t├╢nten rauschend eure Lieder zu, und K├╝he haben ihn mit ihrer Milch gew├дrmt.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬRadiant Soma, when filtered, pour upon us accusative ulated unwasting nutritious food, which is milked for us three times a day, without hindrance, giving forth a sound, yielding strength and delight and fair male offspring.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

O Soma, o drop, purifying yourself, bring us continuous, swelling, unfailing refreshment by purifying yourself,
(refreshment) that, never drying up, will milk out for us three times a day an abundance of good heroes, along with cattle, prizes,
and honey.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the functional contrast between ─Б╠БтАж pavasva and adjacent p├бvam─Бnaс╕е.

+Griffith

O Soma, Indu, while they cleanse thee, pour on us accumulateds Plentiful, nutritious food,
Which, ceaseless, thrice a day shall yield us hero power enriched with store of nourishment, and strength, and Meath.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe all-obsergant Soma, the showerer (of the desires) of his eulogists, the increase of the day, the dawn, the sun; maker of rivers he desires to enter the pitchers, penetrating to Indra’s heart, (praised) by the wise.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The bull of the thoughts, wide gazing, purifies himselfтАФSoma, the lengthener of day, of dawn, of heaven.
Through the action of the rivers he has made the tubs bellow, entering the heart of Indra through (the action of) the inspired ones.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

тАЬBull of the thoughtsтАЭ (vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б mat─лn─Б╠Бm) is a slightly odd expression, but it fits the pattern of IX.76.4 pit─Б╠Бmat─лn─Б╠Бm, 96.5 janit─Б╠Бmat─лn─Б╠Бm, 103.4 net─Б╠Бmat─лn─Б╠Бm, though without obvious agentive content here тАФalthough Geldner interpr. тАШbullтАЩ as тАШBefruchterтАЩ.

The three genitives with pratar─лt─Б╠Бby all the standard accounts (incl. the published

tr., also Ober II.53) consist of two temporal expressions (day, dawn) and a spatial one (heaven). It is not clear to me what тАЬlengthening/extending heavenтАЭ would involve, and so, though gen./abl. div├бс╕е is almost always тАШheavenтАЩ rather than тАШdayтАЩ, I now wonder if it here refers to тАШdayтАЩ. Other passages containing both тАШdayтАЩ words include III.56.6 tr├нr ─Б╠Бdiv├бс╕е savitar v─Б╠Бry─Бс╣Зi, div├й-diva ─Б╠Бsuva tr├нr no ├бhnaс╕е тАЬThree times a day, every day, o Savitar, impel valuables to us, three times dailyтАЭ; X.7.4 dy├║bhiс╕е тАж ├бhabhiс╕е; X.12.4 ├бh─Б y├бd dy─Б╠Бvaс╕е тАж ├бyan тАФ and, interestingly enough, two expressions in this very hymn, vss. 41 and 42, on which see further ad locc. The question is what, if anything, is the semantic distinction between the two тАШdayтАЩ words div- / dyu- and ├бhar / ├бhan-. In principle тАЬdaytimeтАЭ (versus night time) could be distinguished from the 24-hour day. Which, then, would be which? Assuming that PIE *d ie╠п u-╠п (and its descendents) referred esp. to the bright sky, we might expect the тАШdayтАЩ occurrences of div- / dyu- to refer to the bright day, i.e., day versus night, leaving ├бhar for the 24-hour day. And the numerous exx. of n├бktam (тАж) div─Б╠Б(and reverse order) тАЬby night and by dayтАЭ (I.24.10, 12, 34.2, 98.2, etc., etc.) seem to bear out this prediction. We also find div- / dyu- contrasted with other words for тАШnightтАЩ: e.g., in the instr. pl. dy├║bhir ├бkt├║bhiс╕е (I.34.8, 112.25, III.31.16), and in other case/no.

pairs I.116.24 d├б┼Ыa r─Б╠Бtr─лс╕е тАж n├бva dy┼л╠Бn, VI.49.10 rudr├бс╣Г d├нv─Б vardh├бy─Б rudr├бm akta├║. However, ├бhar is also commonly found in these contexts. Cf. the cmpd.

ahor─Бtr├б- тАШday and nightтАЩ and expressions like r─Б╠Бtry─Б ├бhnaс╕е (X.129.2), t├нsraс╕е kс╣г├бpas tr├нr ├бh─Б (I.116.4), vy ├аkt┼л╠Бn тАж vy ├бh─Бni (V.54.4), r─Б╠Бtr─лbhiс╕е тАж ├бhabhiс╕е (X.10.9), ├бhobhiс╕етАж akt├║bhiс╕е (X.14.9), akt├║bhyaс╕е тАж ├бhabhyaс╕е (X.89.11). Also passages in which light is put into or created for ├бhar / ├бhan- тАФ e.g., IX.92.5 jy├│tir y├бd ├бhne ├бkс╣Ыс╣Зot. An esp. telling example is X.68.11 r─Б╠Бtry─Бс╣Г t├бmo dadhur jy├│tir ├бhan тАЬThey put darkness in the night (and) light in the day.тАЭ I therefore find myself at something of an impasse, since both words are used contrastively with тАШnightтАЩ, and in a passage containing both тАШdayтАЩ words assigning one sense to the one and the other to the other seems arbitrary. In any case, I now do think that div├бс╕е means тАШdayтАЩ here, and would substitute the tr. тАЬтАж the lengthener of the day, of dawn, of the daytimeтАЭ (having made the arbitrary choice).

On kr─Бс╣З─Б╠Бsee comm. ad I.58.3. In addition to the adv. sense (тАШsuccessfully, effectivelyтАЩ) discussed there, this old instr. can be used with true instr. value: тАШby the actionтАЩ, as here. In his 1903 art. (cited ad I.58.3) Oldenberg (p. 35=Kl Schr. 1113) identifies kr─Бс╣З─Б╠Бhere as a neut. pl., not instr. sg.: тАЬdie Werke der Str├╢me, die Kufen hat er br├╝llen gemacht.тАЭ But by the time of the Noten he instead takes it as instr.: тАЬdurch das Tun der Fl├╝sse.тАЭ This is in fact the standard interpr. of kr─Бс╣З─Б╠Бs├нndh┼лn─Бm here: Geldner тАЬUnter Mitwirkung der Str├╢meтАЭ; Renou тАЬPar lтАЩaction des fleuvesтАЭ; L├╝ders (254) = Geldner, but with (?) inserted after тАЬMitwirkung.тАЭ But this p─Бda is regularly compared by these very same scholars with IX.102.1 kr─Бс╣З─Б╠Б┼Ы├н┼Ыur mah─л╠Бn─Бm. And it is generally agreed that mah─л╠Бn─Бm in that p─Бda refers also to the rivers. But there is a split about where to construe this gen. Geldner (and perhaps by implication Oldenberg) follows the pattern of our passage: тАЬUnter Mitwirkung der grossen (Str├╢me),тАЭ but L├╝ders argues (239, 242), rather persuasively, that mah─л╠Бn─Бm belongs rather with ┼Ы├н┼Ыuс╕е, as тАЬchild of the great (rivers),тАЭ in part on the basis of s├нndhum─Бtar- (IX.61.7) тАШwhose mothers are the rivers.тАЭ He is followed by Renou In the interpr. of the two passages only Geldner is consistent, in taking the gen. with kr─Бс╣З─Б╠Бin both cases. L├╝ders, Renou, and the published translation all construe the gen. differently in the two places. I now think this is wrong and a consistent interpr.

should be made, but I make the opposite choice to GeldnerтАЩs. In the passage here I would supply тАШchildтАЩ as headnoun for s├нndh┼лn─Бm and change the tr. to тАЬThrough his action, (the child) of the rivers тАжтАЭ There are several reasons for my change of heart besides a desire for consistency. For one thing kr─Бс╣З─Б╠Бis never elsewhere construed with a gen. For another, Soma is otherwise the sole subj. of ├бv─лva┼Ыat and doesnтАЩt need any assistance in this action.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe ancient sage (Soma) is purified by the wise, guided by the priests he roars into the receptacles; genitive rating the water of the threefold (Indra), he distils sweet juice to gain Indra’s and V─Бyu’s friendship.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Through the inspired ones the primordial poet purifies himself; guided by men he has roared around the casks.
Engendering the name of Trita, he flows as honey, to create the
partnership of Indra and V─Бyu.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner interpr. pavate as a passive, with man─лс╣г├нbhiс╕е as agent (тАЬVon den Verst├дndigen wird der allerste Seher gel├дutertтАЭ), but p├бvate is so insistently reflexive in the Soma maс╣Зс╕Нala that I strongly resist a passive here. RenouтАЩs tr. is like mine, though he doesnтАЩt comment.

Trita is the ur-Soma presser. See disc. ad IX.37.4. Here, as Geldner (n. 20c) suggests, Soma re-creates him for the current pressing, to ensure that Indra and V─Бyu will get their soma.

+Griffith

On, with the prudent singers, flows the ancient Sage and guided by the men hath roared about the vats.
Producing Trita’s name, may he pour forth the meath, that Vayu and that Indra may become his Friends.

+Geldner

Von den Verst├дndigen wird der allererste Seher gel├дutert; von den M├дnnern gez├╝gelt hat er die Kufe umwiehert. Den Namen des Trita hervorrufend str├╢mt er S├╝├Яes aus, um Freundschaft mit Indra und Vayu zu schlie├Яen.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬ(It is) he (who), when purified, illumines the dawn; he the maker of the world is (prosperous) for the rivers; this Soma, having milked the thrice seven (cows) of their curds and milk, exhilarating, flows plural asantly to (go to) the heart.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Is prosperous: abhavat = samс╣Ыddho bhavati

+Jamison Brereton

This one here, being purified, has made the dawns shine widely; this one has become the maker of wide space for the rivers.
This one, having milked thrice seven (cows) for his own milk-mixtureтАФ the exhilarating Soma purifies himself in a way dear to the heart.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The first three p─Бdas of this vs. begin ay├бm тАШthis one hereтАЩ.

The thrice seven cows here are also found in IX.70.1, as Geldner (n. 21c) points out. See the seven cows in vs. 25.

+Griffith

He, being purified, hath made the Mornings shine: this, even this is he who gave the rivers room.
He made the Three Times Seven pour out the milky flow: Soma, the Cheerer, yields whate’er the heart finds sweet.

+Geldner

Dieser lie├Я sich l├дuternd die Morgenr├╢ten aufleuchten; dieser war es, der an den Str├╢men freie Bahn schaffte. Dieser hat aus dreimal Sieben die Milch gemolken. Der berauschende Soma kl├дrt sich, dem Herzen zusagend.

+Grassmann

Gereinigt hat die Morgenr├╢then er erhellt, er war es, der den Str├╢men freie Bahnen schuf, Der aus den dreimal sieben K├╝hen Milchtrank sog, dem Herzen lieb, berauschend rieselt Soma hell.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬFlow, Soma, to the heavenly abodes; let forth, O Indu, (proceed) to the pitcher, to the filter; alighting upon Indra’s belly with a noise, guided by the priests, make the sun ascend the sky.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

To the heavenly abodes: i.e., the bellies of the gods

+Jamison Brereton

Purify yourself, Soma, in the heavenly domains, surging into the tub, into the filter, o drop.
Sitting in the belly of Indra, ever roaring, guided by the men, you have made the sun mount in heaven.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Although the Pp. analyzes ─Б╠Бrohayaс╕е as containing an augment (─Б╠Б/ arohayaс╕е), it could equally well have an injunc.: ─Б╠Б/ rohayaс╕е. The latter would fit better with the injunc. v├н rocayat in 21a, just disc.; the former with the other augmented forms of this tс╣Ыca.

+Griffith

Flow, onward, Soma, in thine own celestial forms, flow, Indu, poured within the beaker and the sieve.
Sinking into the throat of Indra with a roar, led by the men thou madest Surya mount to heaven.

+Geldner

L├дutere dich, Soma, an den himmlischen Geburtst├дtten, in den Krug, auf die Seihe ergossen, o Saft, indem du br├╝llend dich in Indra┬┤s Bauch niederl├дssest, von den M├дnnern gez├╝gelt! Du lie├Яest die Sonne am Himmel aufsteigen.

+Grassmann

O riesle, Soma, in den Himmelsst├дtten hell, entsandt, o Indu, in die Seihe zu dem Kelch; Laut wiehernd setzend dich in Indra’s Bauch, gelenkt von M├дnnern hobst die Sonn’ zum Himmel du.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬEffused with the stones, you flow, Indu, into the filter entering the belly of Indra; Soma, the contemplator, you do look upon man (with affection); you did open the cloud for the aс╣Еgirasas.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Or, you did open the mountain-side which concealed the cattled stolen by the Paс╣Зis

+Jamison Brereton

Pressed by the stones, you purify yourself in the filter, o drop, entering the belly of Indra.
You have become one whose gaze is on men, wide-gazing one. Soma, you opened up the cowpen for the Aс╣Еgirases.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The augmented impf. abhavaс╕е is somewhat surprising in this context, because, at least in the published translation, it seems to refer to the recent past, rather than to the mythic past of the following (a)vс╣Ыс╣Зoс╕е. Perhaps, however, it opens the telling of the Vala myth continued in d (and possibly 24ab; see below).

The augment in (a)vс╣Ыс╣Зoс╕е is quite insecure: the Pp restores it, but it is not found in the Saс╣Гhit─Б text and is metrically de trop.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe pious worshippers desirous of preservation have glorified you, Soma, when being purified; the hawk brought you from heaven, Indu, adorned with all praises.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

You, o Soma, purifying yourself, do the very attentive poets applaud as they seek help.
You did the fine-feathered (falcon) carry here from heaven, o drop, you who are adorned all over with all thoughts.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Both hemistichs open with a distracted 2nd sg. acc. pronoun (t u v─Б╠Бm). The accusative of this pronoun is, of course, historically monosyllabic, though distraction is not uncommon in the RV. Here the distraction may have resulted from matching the distracted nominative sg. form that opened the 2nd hemistich of the previous vs., 23c.

The impf. amadan in b is wrongly tr. as a present in the published translation: correct to тАЬdid тАж applaud.тАЭ This may continue the account of the Vala myth, with the тАЬvery attentive poetsтАЭ being the Aс╣Еgirases themselves. It seems unlikely that it is the first action of the soma-stealing myth found in c.

Once again the Pp. analyzes ─Б╠Б/ abharat, but the sequence could instead be ─Б╠Б/ bharat with an injunc.

+Griffith

In thee, O Soma, while thou purifitedst thee, high-thoughted sages, seeking favour, have rejoiced.
Down from the heavens the Falcon brought thee hitherward, even thee, O Indu, thee whom all our hymns adorn.

+Geldner

Dir, wenn du dich l├дuterst, o Soma, jubelten die Redekundigen wohlgesinnt, um Gunst bittend zu. Dich brachte der Falke vom Himmel, o Saft, der mit allen dichterischen Gedanken ausgeschm├╝ckt wird.

+Grassmann

Dir, Soma, jauchzten andachtsvoll die S├дnger zu, nach deiner Gunst verlangend, dir, dem flammenden, Dich, Indu, trug der Adler von dem Himmel her, dich, der durch alle Lieder du verherrlicht wirst.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬSeparate, hundred-streamed, commingling (with the Soma), water-desiring, (the sun’s rays) approach the green-tinted (Soma); the fingers cleanse him pervaded by rays, in the third sphere illumined by the sun.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Hundred-streamed: or, ┼Ыatadh─Бraiс╕е = Soma and juices;

Harim : a reference to Indra;

Abhi┼Ыriyaс╕е = mixed with milk;

Udanyuvaс╕е = desiring (Indra’s rain)

+Jamison Brereton

Inexhaustible, possessing a hundred streams, excelling in beauty [/serving as mixture], they [=mixing waters] roar down to the tawny
one as they provide water.
The fingers groom him wreathed with cows, on the third back, in the luminous realm of heaven.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

On the likely pun on abhi┼Ыr├нyaс╕е, see Geldner (n. 27ab), also Scarlatta 547-48.

It is not entirely clear what тАЬthe third backтАЭ (tс╣Ыt─л╠Бye pс╣Ыс╣гс╣нh├й) refers to, but most likely the highest (third) realm of heaven. Cf., for the back of heaven in general, div├бs pс╣Ыс╣гс╣нh├й in IX.66.5.

+Griffith

The ceaseless watery fountains with their hundred streams sing, as they hasten near, to him the Golden-hued
Him, clad in robes of milk, swift fingers beautify on the third height and in the luminous realm of heaven.

+Geldner

Diese hundertstrahligen, bevorrechteten, wassergebenden Str├╢me rauschen auf den Falben herab. Die Finger putzen den rings in Kuhmilch eingeh├╝llten auf dem dritten R├╝cken, dem Lichtraum des Himmels.

+Grassmann

In hundert Str├╢men unversieglich rauschten hin die warmen Tr├дnke wellenreich zum goldnen Ross; Die Finger streicheln den von Milch umfluteten auf drittem R├╝cken in des Himmels lichter H├╢h.

+Elizarenkova

foremost founder of foundations, o drop.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner and Renou (also Ober II.43) construe t├бva with r├йtasaс╕е (e.g., Geldner тАЬVon deinem himmlischen Samen sind diese Gesch├╢pfeтАЭ). I am reluctant to do so because of the parallelism of t├бvem─Б╠Бс╕е (/ t├║bhyem─Б╠Бс╕е) just noted: all three expressions should be rendered in the same general way. In addition GeldnerтАЩs tr. essentially assumes r├йtasaс╕е is abl., but its companion adj. divy├бsya is stubbornly gen. I would therefore stick to my tr., though slightly modified for clarity to тАЬYours are these offspring of (your) heavenly semen.тАЭ For тАж v├н┼Ыvasya bh├║vanasya r─Бjasi, see 5d, which is identical, and 36d тАж v├н┼Ыvasya bh├║vanasya r─Бj├бse, in an acc. + inf. phrase.

P─Бda c is essentially a restatement of b.

Since dh─Бma-dh─Б╠Б- is an etymological figure, I have rendered it as one, rather than тАШestablisher of domainsтАЩ, vel sim.

+Wilson

+Jamison Brereton

You are the sea, o poet, the all-knowing [/-finding] one; yours are these five regions in your [/their] expansion.
You have carried yourself beyond heaven and earth; yours are the
lights, self-purifying one, and the sun.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The cmpd. vi┼Ыva-v├нd- is ambiguous here. Geldner and Renou both tr. as тАШallknowingтАЩ, and that is favored by the context, since it is immediately followed by the voc. kave (тАШsage poetтАЩ). But the cmpd recurs in the very similar p─Бda, 39c tv├бс╣Г suv─л╠Бro asi soma vi┼Ыvav├нt, and that vs. contains three similarly formed cmpds that surely belong to тИЪvid тАШfindтАЩ: IX.86.39a gov├нt тАж vasuv├нd dhiraс╣Зyav├нt. There the context favors тАШall-findingтАЩ. (Scarlatta treats the two roots тИЪvid together [489], so he is not forced to distinguish.) I suggest, as usual, that itтАЩs a pun.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬPurified Soma, you are purified for the gods in the filter the supporter of the worlds; the chief (priests) desiring (you) lay hold (of you), all these worlds offer themselves to you.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

You, o self-purifying Soma, are purified for the gods in the filter, in the expansion of space.
You did the fire-priests first grasp; to you have all these worlds
submitted themselves.1324 IX.86

+Jamison Brereton Notes

On the expression pav├нtre r├бjaso v├нdharmaс╣Зi and its more succinct variants see comm. ad IX.64.9.

+Griffith

Thou in the filter, Soma Pavamana, art purified to support the region for the Gods.
The chief, the longing ones have sought to hold thee fast, and all these living creatures have been turned to thee.

+Geldner

Du wirst in der Seihe, in der ganzen Ausbreitung des Raums, f├╝r die G├╢tter gel├дutert, Soma Pavamana. Dich nahmen zuerst die Usij in Besitz; dir sind alle diese Welten untergeordnet.

+Grassmann

Gereinigt wirst den G├╢ttern du, o flammender, o Soma, in der Seihe in der L├╝fte Raum, Zuerst ergriffen, Indu, dich die heischenden, und alle diese Wesen streben hin zu dir.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe sounding (Soma) passes through the woollen fleece; the green-tinted showerer cries in the waters; the worshippers desiring (the Soma) praise him together, the laudations soothe the infant as he cries.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The husky-voiced one goes forth across the sheepтАЩs fleece; the tawny bull has roared down into the woods [/wooden vessels].
The hymnic visions, bellowing [/in their longing], have roared together. The thoughts lick the child who always excites wonder.

+Griffith

Onward the Singer travels o’er the fleecy sieve. the Tawny Steer hath bellowed in the wooden vats.
Hymns have been sung aloud in resonant harmony, and holy songs kiss him, the Child who claims our praise.

+Geldner

Der Barde tritt auf und geht durch das Schafhaar, der Bulle br├╝llt herab auf das Holzgef├д├Я, der Falbe. Die Gebete ert├╢nen laut br├╝llend zusammen, die Lieder lecken das schreiende Junge.

+Grassmann

Der S├дnger schreitet durch die Widder wolle vor, und nach den Fluten wiehert laut der goldne Hengst; Gebete laut ert├╢nend stimmen mit ihm ein, und Lieder k├╝ssen den bewundrungswerthen Spross.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬHe invests himself with the rays of the sun stretching out the triple thread in the way he knows; guiding the recent adorations of the truthful (worshipper), the protection of women passes to the consecrated (vessel).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

He has enveloped himself with the rays of the sun, stretching his own threefold thread, in the way that is known.
Leading the newer directives of truth, as a husband he proceeds to the rendezvous with his wives.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Although the standard interpr. of y├бth─Б vid├й here makes Soma subj. of the verb (e.g., Geldner тАЬwie er es verstehtтАЭ), p─Бda-final y├бth─Б vid├й is a common tag (I.127.4, 132.2, etc.) with a passive reading of the verb: тАЬas is known, in the way that is known.тАЭ The тАЬdirectives of truthтАЭ (с╣Ыt├бsya pra┼Ы├нс╣гaс╕е) are convincingly identified as the hymns by L├╝ders (469-70), as the adj. n├бv─лyas-, a standard descriptor of hymns in the fem., suggests.

I assume that the тАЬthreefold threadтАЭ (t├бntum тАж trivс╣Ыt├бm) refers to the three soma pressings.

+Griffith

He hath assumed the rays of Surya for his robe, spinning, as he knows bow, the triply-twisted thread.
He, guiding to the newest rules of Holy Law, comes as the Women’s Consort to the special place.

+Geldner

Er umkleidet sich mit den Sonnenstrahlen, den dreifachen Faden ausspannend, wie er es versteht. Der Opferordnung Vorschriften aufs neue leitend geht er als Gatte zum Treffort seiner Frauen.

+Grassmann

Er hat sich mit der Sonne Strahlen rings umh├╝llt, den dreigetheilten Faden webend, wie gewohnt; Des Opfers neuste Ordnung leitend eilet er als Gatte hin zu seiner Frauen Brautgemach.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬPurified (Soma), you pour forth abundant juice; like the wonderful sun (you approach) the fleecy filters; purified by the hands of the priests, expressed with the stones you flow for a mighty wealth-yielding conflict.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Purifying yourself as a great flood, brilliant like the sun, you run across the fleecy filters.
Hand-purified by the men, pressed by the stones, you dash for the great rich prize.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The published translation does not make sufficiently clear (or clear at all) that p├бvam─Бna is a voc. Better tr. тАЬSelf-purifying one, as a great flood you run тАжтАЭ With Geldner and Renou I take m├бhy ├бrс╣Зaс╕е тАЬgreat floodтАЭ as a nom., coreferential with the 2nd sg. subj. The statement тАЬyou are the seaтАЭ (29a tv├бс╣Г samudr├│ asi) gives semantic support to the coreferential reading, though the two words (samudr├б- and ├бrс╣Зas-) are different. By contrast, L├╝ders (204, 239; sim. Ober II.152 n. 111) takes it as acc. of extent, indicating the space that the soma traverses, with the тАЬfiltersтАЭ of b parallel to it in a simile: тАЬdu durchl├дufst die grosse Flut, wie die strahlende Sonne die wollenen Seihen.тАЭ This interpr. requires that the real filter (the sheepтАЩs fleece) that the real soma ordinarily traverses be part of the simile, expressing what the sun crosses, while the metaphorical filter (тАЬthe great floodтАЭ) is part of the frame, where the real soma is crossing it. This is either very clever poetics, with several levels of metaphor below the surface simile - or an indication that his interpr. is incorrect. IтАЩm afraid that I incline towards the latter view.

The expression in c g├бbhasti-p┼лto nс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е is somewhat curious, since it essentially provides two agents, or agent-like elements, for the p┼лt├б- ppl.: the 1st cmpd member g├бbhasti- and the indep. instr. nс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е. (Of course, the men are the agents whose hands are the instruments.) Without the тАШhandтАЩ (g├бbhasti-) we would expect *nс╣Ы╠е╠Б-p┼лta-, like nс╣Ы╠Б-dh┼лta- (1x), nс╣Ы╠Б-с╣г┼лta- (1x)(which, oddly enough, both rhyme with our putative form). Renou has a slightly different interpr., but it has the same configuration. His тАЬpress├й par les seigneurs ├а lтАЩaide des pierresтАЭ construes nс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е with what follows, the instr. ├бdribhiс╕е and the ppl. sut├бс╕е, with the two instr. filling the agent and instrument slots respectively. Since nс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е is stationed exactly in between the two instrument+ppl. expressions, thereтАЩs no way to tell - though it seems to me somewhat more elegant for nс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е to double a cmpd. member rather than morphologically doubling another instrument. Note that ├бdri-с╣гuta- is also attested (2x) and that the same ├бdribhiс╕е sut├бс╕е as here is found in this hymn in 23a..

+Griffith

Fain to be cleansed, thou, Pavamana, pourest out, like wondrous Surya, through the fleece, an ample sea.
Purified with the hands, pressed by the men with stones, thou speedest on to mighty booty-bringing war.

+Geldner

O Pavamana, als gro├Яe Flut rinnst du farbenpr├дchtig wie die Sonne durch die Filter aus Schafwolle. Von M├дnnern mit den H├дnden gel├дutert, mit Steinen ausgeschlagen rinnst du zu gro├Яem gl├╝ckbringendem Gewinn.

+Grassmann

Im Flammenstrom durchrieselst du das grosse Meer, wie Sonnenglanz im hellen Strome durch das Sieb, Gekl├дrt vom Arm der M├дnner und vom Stein gepresst, ergiesst du dich zu grossem, beutereichem Gut.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYou rush, Pavam─Бna, to (bring) food and strength; you alight on the pitchers like a falcon on its nest; (you) the exhilarating effused juice giving exhilaration to Indra, resembling the support of heaven, beholding (all things).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Self-purifying one, you rush toward refreshment and nourishment. Like a falcon in the woods, you sit in the tubs.
For Indra is pressed the exhilarative, exhilarating drink of exhilaration, the utmost prop of heaven, wide-gazing.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The accumulation of тИЪmad derivatives is striking: m├бdv─Б m├бdyo m├бdaс╕е. The last, m├бda-, is of course extraordinarily common, and the 2nd m├бdya- reasonably well established (13x). But madv├бn- is found only twice.

+Griffith

Thou, Pavamana, sendest food and power in streams. thou sittest in the beakers as a hawk on trees,
For Indra poured as cheering juice to make him glad, as nearest and farseeing bearer-up of heaven.

+Geldner

Du str├╢mst zu Labsal und St├дrkung, o Pavamana; wie der Falke auf die B├дume setzest du dich in die Kr├╝ge, f├╝r Indra als begeisternder, berauschender Trank ausgepre├Яt, des Himmels h├╢chster Pfeiler, weitschauend.

+Grassmann

Hell flammend str├╢mest Speise du und Trank herbei, und setzt dich in die Kufen wie ins Laub der Aar, Zur Lust gepresst dem Indra und zu kr├дft’gem Rausch, des Himmels h├╢chste St├╝tze, weithinschauender!

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe seven sister mothers approach the new-born, victorious sagacious infant, Soma, abiding amidst the waters, supporter of water, divine the contemplator of men to make him the ruler of the whole world.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The seven sister mothers: i.e., the seven rivers clothe the Soma with their water

+Jamison Brereton

The seven sisters, as mothers, (go) to the newborn child of worthy birth, who is attentive to poetic inspiration,
the heavenly Gandharva of the waters, whose gaze is on menтАФto Soma, for the regulation of all creation.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Who the seven sisters (bzw. mothers) are is a matter of dispute: S─Бyaс╣Зa.: the streams or rivers, Geldner: thoughts, Renou (flg. L├╝ders 246): celestial streams/rivers. No one seems to cite the seven milk-cows (sapt├б dhen├бvaс╕е) in vs. 25 of this same hymn, or their multiplied number (thrice seven) in 21. But in this hymn тАЬcowsтАЭ seems the mostly likely immediate referent, esp. given the image of maternal care, whatever those cows may otherwise represent (beyond the milk-mixture).

On the expression in the last p─Бda, see similar phrases in vss. 5 and 28.

+Griffith

The Sisters Seven, the Mothers, stand around the Babe, the noble, new-born Infant, skilled in holy song,
Gandharva of the floods, divine, beholding men, Soma, that he may reign as King of all the world.

+Geldner

Sieben Schwestern kommen als M├╝tter zu dem neugeborenen Hauskind, dem redekundigen, dem himmlischen Gandharva der Gew├дsser mit dem Herrenauge, zu dem Soma, damit er ├╝ber die ganze Welt herrsche.

+Grassmann

Die M├╝tter, sieben Schwestern eilen hin zum Spross, dem neugebornen, herrlichen, begeisterten, Dem m├дnnerschaunden, himmlischen, der Fluten Herrn, dem Soma, dass er herrsche ├╝ber alle Welt.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYou, Soma, are everywhere, the contemplator of men; you, Pavam─Бna, the showerer, hasten to these (waters); do you pour forth upon us (wealth), comprising various treasures and gold; may we be (able) to live in the worlds.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

You, Soma, are one whose gaze is on men on every side. Purifying yourself, bull, you run across these (worlds).
Purify yourself in a manner rich in goods and gold for us. May we be (fit) to live in the worlds.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I take the -mat and -vat forms adverbially.

+Griffith

O Soma, thou beholdest men from every side: O Pavamana, Steer, thou wanderest through these.
Pour out upon us wealth in treasure and in gold: may we have strength to live among the things that be.

+Geldner

Du richtest nach allen Seiten dein Herrenauge, Soma, Pavamana, du Bulle durcheilst diese Welten. L├дutere du uns Besitz von Gut und Gold zu! Wir wollen unter den Gesch├╢pfen zu leben ausersehen sein.

+Grassmann

Du bist, o Soma, m├дnnerschauend ├╝berall, du Stier durchstr├╢mst hellleuchtend diese ganze Welt; So riesle du uns reiches Gut und Gold herbei, und langes Leben werd’ uns in der Welt zu Theil.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

+Jamison Brereton

Purify yourself, as finder of cattle, of goods, of gold. Depositing seed, o drop, you are fitted into the worlds.
You, Soma, are rich in good heroes, finder of all [/all-knowing]. These inspired poets here reverently approach you with a hymn.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

On vi┼Ыvav├нd- see comm. ad vs. 29. Geldner takes it as тАШall-knowingтАЩ here, but the other -v├нd- cmpds in the vs. favor тАШall-findingтАЩ. Renou, like me, тАШall-findingтАЩ here, though тАШall-knowingтАЩ in 29.

+Griffith

Winner of gold and goods and cattle flow thou on, set as impregner, Indu, mid the worlds of life.
Rich in brave men art thou, Soma, who winnest all: these holy singers wait upon thee with the song.

+Geldner

L├дutere dich, Rinder, Gut, Gold ausfindig machend, Samen gebend, o Saft, ├╝ber die Welten gesetzt! Du bist der allwissende Meister, Soma; dir warten diese Redekundigen mit Loblied auf.

+Grassmann

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe wave of the swee-flavoured (Soma) exfites voices (of praise); clothed in water the mighty one plural nges (into the pitcher); the king whose chariot is the filter mounts for the conflict, and, armed with a thousand weapons, wins ample sustenance (for us).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The wave of honey has raised (our?) desires; clothing himself in waters, the buffalo plunges through them.
The king whose chariot is the filter has mounted the prize. He of a thousand spikes wins lofty fame.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

van├бn─Б- is a hapax, though there seems to be general agreement that it means something like тАШdesireтАЩ, derived from the seс╣н root тИЪvani тАШlove, hold dearтАЩ.

There is an Oldenberg Avestan hapax of the same shape (Y. 44.15) that seems unconnected, in that, contextually, the standard tr. тАШvictoryтАЩ seems correct, and it should therefore be derived from aniс╣н тИЪvan тАШwinтАЩ. But Kellens-Pirart in their OA lexicon (1990) equate it directly with our van├бn─Б- and gloss it тАШcharmeтАЩ - which makes no contextual sense and can, I think, easily be dismissed. In any case it is easy to see how our form came to be built. It is the object of the verb ├║d тАж atiс╣гс╣нhipat тАШmade to stand up / raised upтАЩ. The next vs., 41a, has a very similar VP, bhand├бn─Б ├║d iyarti, where the verb is semantically equivalent to our verb and has the same preverb, and the nominal object is a fem. acc. pl. -├бn─Б- form, which provided the template for van├бn─Б-. Given this parallelism and given the fact that the phrase in vs. 41 has to do with granting blessings to us, I think it likely that the desires Soma raised in 40a are our own (so also Geldner, Renou), which he will fulfill in the next vs. v├н g─Бhate as in 8a; cf. also ├бti g─Бhate in 26a.

Soma is presumably тАЬthousand-spikedтАЭ (sah├бsrabhс╣Ыс╣гс╣нi-) because of the knobs, thorns, or similar extrusions on the plant.

+Griffith

The wave of flowing meath hath wakened up desires: the Steer enrobed in milk plunges into the streams.
Borne on his chariot-sieve the King hath risen to war, and with a thousand rays hath won him high renown.

+Geldner

Die Welle der S├╝├Яigkeit hat unser Begehren erregt, in Wasser sich kleidend taucht der B├╝ffel hinein. Als ein K├╢nig, dessen Wagen die Seihe ist, hat er den Siegerpreis erklommen, als der Tausendzackige gewinnt er hohen Ruhm.

+Grassmann

Des Methes Welle hat erhoben ihr Begehr, in Flut gekleidet taucht der B├╝ffel sich hinein; Der K├╢nig fahrend auf der Seihe drang zum Preis, gewinnt, bewehrt mit tausend Dolchen, hohen Ruhm.

рд╕рдГ рд╕реЛрдордГ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдпреБрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рдЧрдиреНрддрд╛ рд╕реЛрдордГ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рд╡рддреАрдГ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рд░реВрдкрдлрд▓рджрд╛рддреНрд░реАрдГ рд╕реБрднрд░рд╛рдГ рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рд╣реНрд░рд┐рдпрдорд╛рдгрд╛рдГ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдГ рднрдиреНрджрдирд╛рдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддреАрдГ рдЙрджрд┐рдпрд░реНрддрд┐ рдЙрддреНрдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрдВ рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдпрддрд┐ ред рдХрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рдХрд╛рд▓реЗ рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдЕрд╣рд░реНрджрд┐рд╡рд┐ рдЕрд╣реЛрд░рд╛рддреНрд░рдпреЛрд╢реНрдЪ ред рдЕрде рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рдХреГрддрдГ ред рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо рдкрд░рд┐рд╡реГрдврдВ рдХрд░реНрдо рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рд╡рддреН рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рднрд┐рд░реНрдпреБрдХреНрддрдореН ред рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдлрд▓рдХрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдЕрдиреНрдирдВ рддрдЪреНрдЪ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рд╡рддреН рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рджреНрдпреБрдкреЗрддрдореН ред рддрдерд╛ рд░рдпрд┐рдВ рдзрдирдореН ред рдХреАрджреГрд╢рдореН ред рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рдкрд╕реНрддреНрдпрдВ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрддрдЧреГрд╣рдореН ред рддрджреБрднрдпрдВ рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреЛ рджреАрдкреНрдд рд╕реЛрдо рдкреАрддрдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░реЗрдг рдкреАрддрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рддрдореЗрд╡ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдорд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рдпрд╛рдЪрддрд╛рддреН рдпрд╛рдЪрд╕реНрд╡ рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe all-pervading (Soma) exfites both day and night all praises easily borne, productive of prosperity; Indu, when drunk, solicit Indra (to give) us food productive of progeny and riches filling our homes.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

He rouses all blessings, consisting of offspring and easy to bear, through our whole lifetime, day upon day. Then, o drop, when drunk, on our behalf beg Indra for a sacred
formulation bringing offspring and for wealth consisting of horses in the homestead.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

On the relation between the first hemistich and vs. 40 see immed. above.

The published translation тАЬтАж all blessings, consisting of offspring and easy to bearтАЭ is awkward and hard to parse. It might be better as тАЬтАж all blessings, consisting of offspring - a light burden -,тАЭ with subh├бra- used in almost jocular fashion. It can simultaneously also refer to тАЬeasy birth,тАЭ with ref. to praj─Б╠Бvat─лс╕е.

The unusually formed (pseudo-)─Бmreс╕Нita ├бhar-divi тАШevery day, day upon dayтАЩ is esp. interesting in light of the discussion of the two тАШdayтАЩ words ad vs. 19 above. It must be a substitute for the more orthodox ─Бmreс╕Нita ├бhar-ahar (6x) for metrical reasons: the standard cmpd. is metrically awk. With three light syllables in a row, it certainly wonтАЩt fit in any cadence and would be difficult anywhere in the vs. line but where itтАЩs always found, p─Бda-initial (which isnтАЩt all that great either - openings with light syllables in both 2 and 3, not to mention 1 and possibly 4, are quite irregular; see Arnold pp 194-95). It is puzzling, however, that the well-attested (47x) (also somewhat aberrantly formed) ─Бmreс╕Нita to the second тАШdayтАЩ stem here, namely div├йdive, was not used in our vs., since it would fit the cadence perfectly and is quite common in Jagat─л cadences. In any case, at least ├бhar-divi suggests that thereтАЩs no clearcut difference of meaning or reference between ├бhar- and the forms of div-/dyuthat mean тАШdayтАЩ.

In the 2nd hemistich, Soma is not asked directly for benefits, but rather urged to intercede with Indra - to beg him for our sake - for offspring and wealth. This displacement is made all the stranger by the use of a тАЬfuture imperative,тАЭ y─Бcat─Бt, which properly should follow another impv. Perhaps the displacement in time that such an impv. represents - that is, there should be an intervening impv. before it - indirectly reflects the displacement in person - that is, Soma is the middleman, intervening between us and Indra. I suppose it is bad form to ask Indra directly in a hymn devoted to Soma.

There is further displacement here. The тАЬsacred formulation bringing offspringтАЭ (br├бhma praj─Б╠Бvat) that we want Soma to get Indra to give us is not a direct request for Indra to bestow offspring on us, but rather for him to inspire in us a formulation that we can then offer to him, which will, only then, result in offspring.

ItтАЩs a long and winding road to what we want! The interpr. of the hapax bahuvr. ├б┼Ыva-pastya- is disputed. My tr. тАЬconsisting of horses in the homesteadтАЭ essentially follows GrassmannтАЩs тАШRosse im Stalle habendтАЩ, though it would be more lit. as тАШhaving a homestead that has horses in itтАЩ - a v├бjrab─Бhu- type cmpd. GeldnerтАЩs tr. тАЬan vielen RossenтАЭ seems to evade the issue, but his statement in n. 41c тАЬwie sp├дter -┼Ы─Бlin-тАЭ is more forthcoming: -┼Ы─Бlin- means lit.

тАШhaving a house/roomтАЩ, but develops to тАШabounding inтАЩ. Nonetheless, I find it hard to believe that a RVic poet would go to the trouble of using a fairly rare word as 2nd member, only in order to bleach it of its particular meaning. RenouтАЩs тАЬla richesse qui r├йside dans les chevauxтАЭ (and OberтАЩs тАЬdessen fester Wohnsitz Pferde sindтАЭ [I.537 n.

111]) employs an abstract sense of pasty├а- to characterize where wealthтАЩs dwelling is: it resides in - that is, is founded on / consists of тАФ horses. Whereas my interpr.

assumes a concrete homestead, which belongs to the speaker and/or his associates, that is stuffed, as it were, with horses. The difference between the abstract and the concrete interpr. is small but significant, and I continue to prefer the concrete one.

+Griffith

Dear to all life, he sends triumphant praises forth, abundant, bringing offspring, each succeeding day.
From Indra crave for us, Indu, when thou art quaffed, the blessing that gives children, wealth that harbours steeds.

Er bringt zeitlebens Tag f├╝r Tag alle l├╢blichen Dinge, die Nachwuchs haben, auf, deren Last leicht ist: Getrunken sollst du, Saft, f├╝r uns den Indra um Segen, der Nachwuchs bringt, um Reichtum an vielen Rossen bitten.

Er l├дsst erstehen kinderreiche Segnungen, die alle stark sind, allbelebend Tag f├╝r Tag, Geschl├╝rft, o Indu, geh den Indra f├╝r uns an um kinderreich Gebet und rossereichen Stall.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAt the beginning of the day the green-tinted delightful exhilarating (Soma) is recognized by the intelligence (of the praisers) and by their praises; approaching the two men he passes in the midst (of heaven and earth, bestowing) upon the upholder (of the rite) both human and divine (riches).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The two men: i.e., the praiser and the worshipper; or, secular and sacred people (laukikavaidikau)

+Jamison Brereton

At the vanguard of the days [=dawn] the tawny, delightful, exhilarating drink makes himself conspicuous with his appearance through the days. Setting in place the two peoples [=gods and men], he speeds between them in upholding the тАЬpraise of menтАЭ and the heavenly (praise).

+Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs., too, contains the two тАШdayтАЩ words, gen. pl. ├бhn─Бm, dependent on ├бgre, and the adverbial instr. expression ├бnu dy├║bhiс╕е. See comm. ad vss. 19, 41.

English translation:

тАЬ(The priests) smear and grease and anoint (the Soma with milk); (the gods) taste the invigorating (juice); they smear it over with sweet (milk). Purifying it with gold, they plural nge it into those (waters) the sprinkler, the beholder, falling into the seething torrent.тАЭ

Smear and grease and anoint: a├▒jate, vya├▒jate and sama├▒jate are synonyms; into the seething torrent: sindhor ucchv─Бse = liс╣н, in the hreathing of the river; i.e., going to an elevated plural ce, the receptacle of the juice, rasasy─Бdh─Бrabh┼лte ucchrite de┼Ыe gacchantam

+Jamison Brereton

They anoint himтАФanoint him separately and jointly. They lick (him who is) resolve; they anoint him with honeyтАФ
him, the ox flying in the burbling up of the river. (The waters,) who

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich is striking with its series of identical verbs in p─Бda a, with p─Бda b ending with the same verb: a├▒j├бte vy ├а├▒jate s├бm a├▒jate, тАж abhy ├а├▒jate.

The first p─Бda lacks a syllable (rest at 4); as Oldenberg suggests, the metrical irregularity is most likely meant to call attention to the word play.

Geldner, Renou, L├╝ders (239) take the various verbs as reflex., with Geldner (n. 43ab) taking the subj. as the soma-drinking singers and Renou as the waters. But though mid. тИЪa├▒j is probably more often reflex./pass. than trans., it can be the latter, and that makes more sense here. Cf., e.g., IX.97.57 s├бm a├▒jate r┼лp├бm тАЬthey jointly anoint his form,тАЭ and recall the many times in this maс╣Зс╕Нala in which soma тАЬis anointed,тАЭ using the true passive ajy├бte (-se) (often as a pun with тАШis drivenтАЩ to тИЪaj). See especially in the next tс╣Ыca of this hymn 47c g├│bhiс╕е тАж samajy├бse, in the same metrical position as s├бm a├▒jate here. I supply the default Soma as obj. throughout the first hemistich; he is found as explicit (though metaphorical) obj. in the 2nd hemistich. As for the subj. of all these verbs, I agree with Renou that it is the waters.

The тАЬox flying in the burbling up of the riverтАЭ of p─Бda c is an ex. of the layers of metaphor just alluded to above: it compresses three different representations of Soma into a single image.

I take the subj. of gс╣Ыbhс╣Зate and referent of hiraс╣Зya-p─Бv─Б╠Бс╕е in d still to be the waters, with ─Бsu functioning as reflexive. Renou explicitly changes his subj. here to тАЬles hommes.тАЭ

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬSing (you priests) to the intelligent Pavam─Бna; like a mighty shower he sends forth food; like a snake he glides out of his old skin, sporting like a horse he hastens forth, the showerer, green-tinted.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Sing to the self-purifying one who is attentive to poetic inspiration. Like a great stream he rushes beyond his stalk;
like a snake he slinks beyond his withered skin. Playful like a steed, the tawny bull has run.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner, Renou, Ober (II.54) take ├бndhaс╕е as nom., parallel to dh─Б╠Бr─Б in the simile.

But insofar as it is possible to narrow the referent of this word, it is used of the stalk of the soma (see comm. ad IV.1.19). I take it here as acc., construed with ├бti. This p─Бda, like the following one, depicts the soma juice leaving behind the solid parts of the plant, and ├бti тАШbeyondтАЩ is used in both p─Бdas to express the material beyond which the soma juice has gone.

The simile in d, ├бtyo n├б kr─лс╕╖an, is also found in 26d.

+Griffith

Sing forth to Pavamana skilled in holy song: the juice is flowing onward like a mighty stream.
He.glideth like a serpent from his ancient skin, and like a playful horse the Tawny Steer hath run.

+Geldner

Lobsinget dem redekundigen Pavamana! Wie ein gro├Яer Strom rinnt der Saft durch die Seihe. Wie eine Schlange entkriecht er der alten Haut; wie ein Renner spielend ist der bullenhafte Falbe geflossen.

+Grassmann

Dem rieselnden, begeisterten singt Lobgesang, dem grossen Strome gleichend rinnt er durch das Kraut, Der Schlange gleichend schl├╝pft er durch die alte Haut, wie Renner h├╝pfend eilt dahin der goldne Hengst.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬ(Soma) going foremost, radiant, sanctified by water, plural ced in the firmament as the measure of days is glorified; green-tinted, shedding water, of goodly aspect, the source of moisture, borne in a chariot of light he flows giving wealth, friendly to the house.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The measure of days: beacause, the rule as to the length of day depends on the increase and decrease of the moon’s digits, Soma being here regarded as the moon

+Jamison Brereton

Going in the vanguard, the king who is found in the waters displays his power, the measure(r) of the days, fitted into the worlds.
The ghee-backed fallow bay, a flood lovely to see, having light as his chariot, accustomed to wealth, purifies himself.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

In a agre-g├бс╕е echoes ├бgre ├бhn─Бm in 42a; in our vs. ├бhn─Бm appears in the following p─Бda, dependent on something else (vim─Б╠Бnaс╕е), though Renou supplies it with agreg├бс╕е as well.

bh├║vaneс╣гv ├бrpitaс╕е also in 39b.

In d I construe r─Бy├й with oky├ас╕е, although I cannot find any parallel usage. But on its own, oky├ас╕е is hard to fit semantically into the vs.; cf. GeldnerтАЩs тАЬgern bleibendтАЭ and RenouтАЩs тАЬ(ce dieu) domestique,тАЭ which seem like afterthoughts..

+Griffith

Dweller in floods, King, foremost, he displays his might, set among living things as measurer of days.
Distilling oil he flows, fair, billowy, golden-hued, borne on a car of light, sharing one hom-e with wealth.

+Geldner

Vorangehend zeigt der im Wasser wohnende K├╢nig seine St├дrke, der Ausmesser der Tage, ├╝ber die Welten gesetzt. Ein Falbe, der Schmalz auf dem R├╝cken tr├дgt; dessen Wagen Licht ist, sch├╢n von Aussehen, l├дutert er sich flutend zu Reichtum, gern bleibend.

+Grassmann

Der Fluten K├╢nig, f├╝hrend sie, erweist sich stark, die Tage messend, in die Wesen eingef├╝gt; Das sch├╢ne Ross, das wallende mit Fett bedeckt, den Lichtschein fahrend, str├╢mt als Hausherr reiches Gut.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe supporter of heaven the prepared exhilarating (Soma) is let loose, the triple (beverage) rushes to the waters; the worshippers taste the sounding Soma juice, when the reciters of holy texts approach the embodied (beverage) with praise.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Triple beverage: tridh─Бtu = three vessle, the droс╣Зakala┼Ыa, ─Бhavan─лya and putabhс╣Ыt; or, just, three metallic ores: gold, silver, lead/coopper

+Jamison Brereton

It has been sent surgingтАФthe prop of heaven, the exhilarating drink held aloft. It rushes threefold around the worlds.
The thoughts lick the plant that always excites wonder, when the
versifiers have come to array it with a hymn.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

In p─Бda a skambh├│ div├бс╕е reminds us of 35d div├│ viс╣гс╣нambh├бс╕е with a diff.

lexical real On tridh─Б╠Бtu- see comm. ad IX.70.8.

P─Бda c aс╣Г┼Ы├║с╣Г rihanti mat├бyaс╕е p├бnipnatam is identical to 31d, save for the first word, which in 31 is ┼Ы├н┼Ыum.

In d y├бdi would be best read y├бd *─л, both for sense and for meter, since an opening with light syllables in positions 3 and 4 before an early caesura is very rare (see Arnold 194).

Geldner tr. nirс╣З├нjam тАж yay├║с╕е as тАЬStaat machenтАЭ (make a show), based, he says (n.

46d), on ┼Ы├║bhaс╣Г y─Б. I see no reason to attenuate the sense of nirс╣З├нj-. As Scarlatta (284- 85) argues, this stem can be both a concrete noun тАШgarmentтАЩ and an infin. тАШto arrayтАЩ.

The infinitival usages he cites are mostly the dat. nirс╣З├нje (which, in all quoted cases, I take as a noun) and he is uncertain about the usage of this acc. ex. But since the analysis just proposed of y├бd *─л provides us with an acc. obj., infinitival usage seems best here.

+Griffith

Loosed is the heavens! support, the uplifted cheering juice: the triply-mingled draught flows round into the worlds.
The holy hymns caress the stalk that claims our praise, when singers have approached his beauteous robe with song.

pressed you sit in the tubs, Soma.
